- diagnosis: Task: infer the most likely AIE mechanism class for C25H24N4 from structure and quickly obtainable baseline quantum descriptors. Current top1 is ICT; runner-up is TICT. The molecule has a strong donor–acceptor architecture (tertiary amine donor; cyano and aza-aryl acceptors; extended π-conjugation) consistent with an ICT bright state whose nonradiative decay in solution can be suppressed upon aggregation (RIM/RIR). Top1 remains uncertain because TICT is also plausible given the available torsional degrees of freedom and the common D–A AIE pattern where a dark/weakly emitting twisted CT minimum forms in solution but is inhibited in aggregates. Evidence to separate ICT vs TICT: baseline S1 state character (CT amount), oscillator strength, and whether the excited state is predisposed to twisting/decoupling; later, an explicit torsional scan or excited-state relaxation would be decisive. Shared prepared structure is available (10 conformers; selected conformer id 5; rotatable bonds=4; high planarity proxy ~0.98). Macro can provide mechanistic priors from structural motifs and known AIE patterns; Microscopic can provide one low-cost baseline S0/S1 calculation to quantify CT/oscillator strength and flag TICT propensity proxies, but will not (this round) do conformer/torsion sensitivity or multi-step workflows. First round should gather both: macro for qualitative mechanism triage and microscopic for quantitative CT/brightness indicators to reweight ICT vs TICT early within the round budget.

Net: structural evidence slightly favors ICT as the baseline (high planarity/rigid core), while retaining credible TICT accessibility due to the nontrivial set of rotatable linkers.

Reasoning summary: From the shared structure context, the molecule is a donor–acceptor conjugated chromophore: a tertiary amine (N-methylpiperazine substituent) connected to an extended aryl–vinyl–aryl system bearing a cyano group and a pyridyl ring (acceptor-rich region). Key macro indicators: (1) high planarity_proxy (~0.978) suggests a largely coplanar conjugated backbone in the selected conformer, consistent with stabilized ICT in solution; (2) rotatable_bond_count=4 with torsion_candidate_count=4 indicates multiple internal torsions capable of forming a twisted charge-transfer geometry (TICT) if one or more D–π or π–A dihedrals can decouple; (3) aromatic_ring_count=3 and ring_system_count=4 indicate a rigid multi-ring core, which generally resists full twisting but still allows localized torsion at linker bonds; (4) compactness_proxy (~0.936) and large principal_span_proxy (~89) together suggest an elongated yet fairly compact conformation—typical of push–pull stilbene-like motifs—supporting strong through-bond conjugation while leaving a few key torsions as the main flexibility. Net: structural evidence slightly favors ICT as the baseline (high planarity/rigid core), while retaining credible TICT accessibility due to the nontrivial set of rotatable linkers.

### Round 4 | planner | planner_diagnosis

- diagnosis: Round 4/20 (remaining incl. current: 17). Top1=ICT (0.68) and Top2=TICT (0.20). Latest evidence (microscopic targeted state characterization) was contracted to proxy-only outputs: it reproduced the same bright S1 (E~3.415 eV, f~1.122) dominated by a single transition (101->102), but failed to deliver NTO/attachment–detachment/transition-density or electron–hole separation/overlap metrics, so it does not directly close ICT vs TICT. This leaves ICT strengthened slightly by consistency/absence of new TICT-positive signatures, while TICT remains unresolved but not reinforced. Key remaining discriminator between ICT vs TICT is whether a twisted CT minimum exists and/or whether excited-state electron–hole localization metrics indicate strong CT with torsion-enabled decoupling. Verifier supplementation is sufficient (ICT__vs__TICT) and remains mixed-but-leaning-ICT; closure justification is still collecting and currently blocked by missing internal CT/localization observables from the attempted characterization route. Best next action is a single microscopic registry action that can produce CT/localization descriptors from available MO artifacts (since current run did not output NTO/transition-density metrics).

- action: microscopic

- confidence: 0.68

- task_instruction: Microscopic: run exactly one registry-backed action `run_targeted_charge_analysis` on the existing artifact bundle `round_04_run_targeted_state_characterization_bundle` (or, if that bundle is not eligible for charge analysis, use `round_01_baseline_bundle`), targeting the same fixed geometry/state window=[1]. Request excited-state-relevant population/charge outputs available in this route (e.g., Hirshfeld/other supported charge partitions per fragment if supported). Do not run any geometry optimization, torsion scans, or excited-state relaxation.

### Round 5 | planner | planner_diagnosis

- diagnosis: Round 5/20 (remaining incl. current: 16). Top1=ICT (0.70), Top2=TICT (0.19); decision/closure pair remains ICT__vs__TICT. Latest evidence (microscopic run_targeted_charge_analysis) did not strengthen or weaken ICT materially because it only returned ground-state dipole and a Hirshfeld-charge table without an S1-vs-S0 (or excitation-associated) charge-redistribution metric; it does, however, confirm again a robust bright lowest state (S1: 3.4154 eV, f=1.122, dominant transition 101->102) at the fixed geometry, which is more compatible with an emissive planar ICT than a dark TICT minimum. TICT is slightly weakened (no new TICT-positive signatures such as dual-state behavior, dark-state proxy, or torsion-enabled alternative state), but remains the main challenger due to untested torsional relaxation. An additional candidate (neutral aromatic) is slightly weakened because the molecule is a strong push–pull D–π–A and external precedent favors CT-involving ICT. Verifier supplementation status is sufficient (high IG, mixed but overall ICT-leaning); closure justification remains collecting because internal CT/localization observables are still missing. Key remaining discriminator: evidence of (a) substantial S1 donor→acceptor charge redistribution / CT localization, or (b) a low-energy twisted CT minimum (TICT) reachable along a torsion coordinate. Next action is best as a single bounded microscopic observable that can directly provide an internal CT proxy (without torsion scans/relaxation).

### Round 6 | planner | planner_diagnosis

- diagnosis: Round 6/20 (remaining incl. current: 15). Top1=ICT (0.73), Top2=TICT (0.16); closure pair remains ICT__vs__TICT. Latest evidence (run_targeted_density_population_analysis) strengthens ICT slightly by adding that density/population observables are available at the same fixed geometry where S1 remains very bright (f~1.122), consistent with an allowed planar emissive state rather than a dark TICT minimum. This does not directly eliminate TICT because torsional relaxation to an unseen twisted minimum is still untested, but it does not add any positive TICT signal either. Neutral-aromatic remains low because the molecule is a strong D–A push–pull system and verifier precedent favors ICT. Remaining key discriminator between ICT vs TICT: whether S1 excitation shows strong donor→acceptor charge redistribution / localization consistent with ICT at (near-)planar geometry, versus evidence that a twisted CT minimum is energetically accessible and would be dark. Verifier supplementation is sufficient (external discriminators and close-family precedent already collected). Closure justification is still collecting because we still lack a quantitative internal CT/localization index; the new density/population outputs need to be converted into an interpretable CT proxy. Next action best now: a single bounded microscopic parse/analysis that can extract an interpretable CT/localization proxy from existing density/population artifacts (or, if unavailable, switch to a different single-action characterization that reliably outputs fragment charge-transfer indices).

- action: microscopic

- confidence: 0.73

### Round 7 | planner | planner_diagnosis

- diagnosis: Round 7/20 (remaining incl. current: 14). Top1=ICT (0.74), Top2=TICT (0.15); closure pair remains ICT__vs__TICT. Latest evidence (microscopic run_targeted_localized_orbital_analysis) confirms availability of localized-orbital artifacts and MO files, while reproducing the same bright lowest S1 (E≈3.415 eV, f≈1.122; dominant transition 101→102). However, it still does not yield an interpretable donor-vs-acceptor localization/CT index (no NTO/attachment–detachment/e–h metrics; localized-orbital content is present but not summarized into a fragment-localization proxy by the route). Thus, the new evidence leaves ICT as the strongest hypothesis (supported by planarity + bright S1 + verifier close-family precedent) and slightly weakens TICT only insofar as no dark/alternate state signature emerges. Key remaining discriminator between ICT and TICT: evidence that twisting accesses a lower-energy (often dark) CT minimum (TICT) vs a predominantly planar emissive CT state (ICT), ideally via torsion sensitivity (snapshot energies/state ordering) or an explicit CT/localization metric. Verifier supplementation: sufficient. Closure justification: still collecting (internal quantitative CT/localization proxy missing). Best next action: a bounded internal torsion-snapshot probe (single action) to test whether twisting along the most relevant D–π/π–A dihedral(s) can substantially reduce oscillator strength / change state ordering, which is a direct ICT vs TICT discriminator within current registry capabilities.

- action: microscopic

- confidence: 0.74

- task_instruction: Microscopic: run exactly ONE registry-backed Amesp action `run_torsion_snapshots` using the existing shared prepared structure (or most recent bundle geometry if required by the action defaults). Target the most TICT-relevant donor–aryl or aryl–vinyl dihedral (the junction that most plausibly decouples donor from the pi-system) and generate a small fixed set of snapshot angles (e.g., 0°, 30°, 60°, 90°). For each snapshot, compute vertical S1 energy and oscillator strength (state_window=[1]). Goal: detect whether twisting produces a low-f (dark) CT-like state or strong state reordering consistent with TICT accessibility. Do not run any excited-state relaxation or solvent model.

### Round 8 | planner | planner_diagnosis

- diagnosis: Round 8/20 (remaining incl. current: 13). Top1=ICT (0.80) and Top2=TICT (0.11). Latest evidence strengthens ICT and weakens TICT: a torsion-snapshot scan on a high-relevance aryl–vinyl dihedral (dih_11_12_13_14; 0°, 30°, 60°, 90°) shows S1 remains the lowest bright state with essentially no torsion sensitivity (excitation spread 0.0059 eV; oscillator-strength spread 0.0004; f≈0.1403–0.1407). This fails to produce the hallmark TICT signal (strong darkening and/or state reordering at large twist) along a key conjugation-breaking coordinate. Neutral-aromatic is slightly reduced by the strong D–A motif and prior precedent but remains a minor alternative because stable brightness across twist can also be LE-like. Verifier supplementation for ICT vs TICT remains sufficient (status=sufficient), and closure justification is still collecting: the key remaining discriminator is whether *other* torsions (not the scanned aryl–vinyl bond) can access a dark twisted CT state and/or whether any direct CT/localization index confirms donor→acceptor charge separation. Given the new direct torsion-insensitivity evidence, the best next action is another single torsion-snapshot test targeting a different high-relevance dihedral (preferably donor–aryl / N-aryl junction) to more completely rule out TICT accessibility.

- action: microscopic

- confidence: 0.8

- task_instruction: Microscopic: run exactly ONE registry-backed Amesp action `run_torsion_snapshots` targeting a *different* rotatable dihedral than dih_11_12_13_14, prioritizing the donor–aryl (N-aryl) junction associated with the piperazine donor if available. Use the same small angle set [0°, 30°, 60°, 90°], fixed-geometry (optimize_ground_state=false), and compute vertical S1 energies and oscillator strengths (state_window=[1]) for each snapshot. Goal: test whether twisting at the donor–aryl junction yields strong f suppression/state reordering consistent with TICT; otherwise further supports ICT. No excited-state relaxation, no solvent.

### Round 9 | planner | planner_diagnosis

- diagnosis: Round budget: 9/20 used, 12 remaining (including current). Top1=ICT (0.86), Top2=TICT (0.07). Latest evidence strengthens ICT and weakens TICT: the new torsion-snapshot scan (dih_29_0_1_2; 0/30/60/90°) again shows torsion_sensitive=false with small spreads (ΔE≈0.0077 eV, Δf≈0.0075) and the lowest state remaining bright across angles, consistent with an emissive ICT manifold rather than access to a dark twisted CT state. This complements the prior aryl–vinyl scan (dih_11_12_13_14) that also showed negligible darkening/state reordering. The top2 challenger (TICT) is further constrained because two independent torsional coordinates fail to reveal the hallmark TICT signature. Remaining key discriminator between ICT vs TICT: whether a true donor–aryl (N-aryl) junction torsion (specifically involving the piperazine-attached aryl bond) can access a dark CT-like state upon twisting (not guaranteed by the medium-relevance heteroaryl-linkage scan), or a direct CT/localization metric (unavailable in prior descriptor routes). Verifier supplementation is sufficient; closure justification is collecting but now substantially stronger due to two torsion-insensitivity results. Best next action is a final targeted torsion-snapshot run that explicitly prioritizes an N-aryl (donor–aryl) dihedral (with preferred_bond_types including N-aryl/aryl-amine linkage if supported) to close the remaining TICT loophole.

### Round 10 | planner | planner_diagnosis

- diagnosis: Round 10/20 (11 remaining incl. current). Top1=ICT (0.82), Top2=TICT (0.12). Latest evidence partially challenges (but does not overturn) ICT: a new torsion-snapshot scan selected dih_11_12_15_16 (aryl–vinyl; relevance=high) after relaxations, and reports torsion_sensitive=true with excitation_energy_ev increasing from 3.4479 (0°) to 3.9794 (90°) and oscillator_strength decreasing from 0.1463 to 0.1209. This indicates torsion affects the vertical excited state, but crucially it does not produce the hallmark TICT signature of an oscillator-strength collapse to ~0 or a dark-state takeover (S1 remains the lowest bright state in the limited state_window=[1]). TICT is therefore slightly strengthened relative to the pre-round-10 belief only because torsion sensitivity exists, yet it remains disfavored overall because (i) earlier torsion scans showed torsion_sensitive=false and no darkening/reordering, and (ii) verifier close-family precedent for planar piperazine push–pull systems supports ICT-like single-band emission and disfavors TICT. Key remaining discriminator: explicitly test the true donor–aryl (N–aryl / aryl-amine) junction torsion (if present) with adequate state coverage (preferably include at least a few states, not only S1) to detect any dark CT state reordering. Verifier supplementation: sufficient. Closure justification: still collecting; the latest scan did not hit the intended donor–aryl junction and used selection relaxations.

- action: finalize

- confidence: 0.82

- final_hypothesis_rationale: Best-available closure keeps 'ICT' ahead of 'TICT', but the repeated microscopic local limitation shows the remaining gap is not shrinking under the current route: Directly probe the donor–aryl (N–aryl / aryl-amine) torsion with sufficient vertical-state coverage to detect possible state reordering into a dark CT state (TICT hallmark).
